## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of chemical concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Standard rate laws express dA/dt as functions of A (power-law, Michaelis-Menten, etc.), while explicit time dependence may arise from time-varying conditions or integrated/coupled dynamics.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combined first and second order terms)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type, reversible or autocatalytic)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type equation)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with back reaction or constant source)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (trimolecular reaction)
- Damped rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy)
- Time-modulated decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (linearly time-varying rate constant)
- Fractional with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (power-law in both concentration and time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative proportionality to concentration (dA_dt = -k*A^n) indicates consumption following an nth-order rate law
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate enzyme-like saturation or surface-limited reactions
- Product of A and (constant - A) indicates autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior in chemical systems
- Explicit time dependence in rate expressions suggests non-isothermal conditions, photolysis, or catalyst deactivation
- Square of concentration in denominator suggests competitive inhibition or Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface mechanisms
- Sum of terms with different powers of A suggests parallel reaction pathways or competing mechanisms
- Exponential functions of A (exp(c*A)) can arise from concentration-dependent activation energies or non-ideal solution effects
- Rate laws with A*(1-A/K) structure indicate approach to equilibrium with carrying capacity K
- Polynomial rate laws (sum of A^n terms) often represent truncated series expansions of complex mechanisms
- If dA_dt depends on t only through A(t), the system is autonomous and the rate law is purely concentration-dependent
